         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202400127-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202400127-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202400127-sec-0030">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202400127-sec-0030-title">2.1 Synthesis of HE Multiphase Materials</h3>
            
            <p>Based on the well-studied structure of Na<sub>0.706</sub>Ni<sub>0.344</sub>Mn<sub>0.653</sub>O<sub>2</sub> three additional elements of Cu, Ti, and Sn are introduced into the TM layer to construct the HE configuration, and the contents of these five types of TMs are optimized to achieve the formation of multiphase structures. In Na<sub>0.706</sub>Ni<sub>0.344</sub>Mn<sub>0.653</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, Ni functions as the electrochemically active element to provide Na-storage capacity,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0005_R_d66350119e757" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv. Energy Mater.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and Mn is used to maintain structural stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0008_R_d66350119e763" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Adv. Mater.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The introduction of Cu is expected to enhance the conductivity and air stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0013_R_d66350119e768" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Ceram. Int. Adv. Mater.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> While the doping of Ti and Sn has been demonstrated to show suppression on the irreversible phase transition.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0010_R_d66350119e773" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Electrochim. Acta Chem. Mater.">10</a>, <a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0022_R_d66350119e773" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - J. Energy Chem.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The stoichiometric ratios of NiO, MnO<sub>2</sub>, CuO, TiO<sub>2</sub>, SnO<sub>2</sub>, and Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (5&nbsp;wt% excess) were ball milled and then sintered at 1000&nbsp;°C for 15&nbsp;h to prepare these cathode materials. By alternating the compositions of Ni(0.2–0.38&nbsp;mol), Mn(0.25–0.64&nbsp;mol), Cu(0–0.15&nbsp;mol), Ti(0–0.2&nbsp;mol), Sn(0–0.25&nbsp;mol), 43 kinds of layered oxide cathodes were prepared, which give the models for exploring the regulations in the formation of HE multiphase structures. From the recorded powder X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns of all these 43 composites, no diffraction peaks of raw materials or impurities were observed (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>–<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information), indicating the successful preparation of HE-layered oxide cathodes. The detailed compositions of these HE-layered structures are shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0001">1a</a>. Considering Mn<sup>4+</sup> owning the smallest radius (r<sub>Mn</sub><sup>4+</sup> = 0.53&nbsp;Å), with the gradual decrease of Mn content and increase in Ni/Cu/Ti/Sn content (r<sub>Ni</sub><sup>2+</sup> = 0.69&nbsp;Å r<sub>Cu</sub><sup>2+</sup> = 0.73&nbsp;Å, r<sub>Ti</sub><sup>4+</sup> = 0.605&nbsp;Å and r<sub>Sn</sub><sup>4+</sup> = 0.69&nbsp;Å), the average size of cation radius at TM site is increased progressively, which is accompanied by the change of phase compositions in multiphase cathodes. In specific, an increased ionic radius of TM leads to a longer bond length of TM-O and a shorter O-O distance between two adjacent TMO<sub>2</sub> layers. As a result, adjacent oxygen and Na are more inclined to form octahedral coordination environments (O3 phase) due to the repulsion in O-O, which is unfavorable to maintaining the trigonal prismatic coordination (P2 phase).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0006_R_d66350119e823" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Phys. B+C Chem. Mater.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Inversely, a smaller O-O repulsion at a lower ion radius allows for the maintenance of prismatic sites (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0001">1b</a>). In HE configuration, due to the presence of five different cations at TM sites, the <i>WAIR</i> of all TMs is employed to investigate the effects of cation radius on phase formation. For example, the <i>WAIR</i> of TMs in Na<sub>0.69</sub>Ni<sub>0.25</sub>Cu<sub>0.07</sub>Mn<sub>0.63</sub>Ti<sub>0.02</sub>Sn<sub>0.02</sub>O<sub>2</sub> is <i>WAIR</i> = 0.25 × r<sub>Ni</sub><sup>2+</sup> + 0.07 × r<sub>Cu</sub><sup>2+</sup> + 0.63 × r<sub>Mn</sub><sup>4+</sup> + 0.02 × r<sub>Ti</sub><sup>4+</sup> + 0.02 × r<sub>Sn</sub><sup>4+</sup> = 0.583 Å. To get a clear relationship between phase structure and <i>WAIR</i>, the structural composition of 43 prepared compounds was listed according to the contents of P2 and O3 phases with the variation of <i>WAIR</i>. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0001">1c</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information), when the <i>WAIR</i> is 0.583 and 0.637&nbsp;Å, the HE oxides display almost only the pure phase of P2 and O3, respectively. When the <i>WAIR</i> falls between 0.583 and 0.637&nbsp;Å, multiphase structures containing P2 and O3 phases were generated. It is observed that <i>WAIR</i> = 0.624&nbsp;Å is a demarcation point (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information), showing the same content of P2 and O3 phases. For instance, in Na<sub>0.7</sub>Ni<sub>0.25</sub>Cu<sub>0.10</sub>Mn<sub>0.40</sub>Ti<sub>0.07</sub>Sn<sub>0.18</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.66</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Cu<sub>0.12</sub>Mn<sub>0.4</sub>Ti<sub>0.08</sub>Sn<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with the same <i>WAIR</i> of 0.624&nbsp;Å, the P2:O3 ratios are 51.40:48.60 and 50.82:49.18, respectively. A smaller <i>WAIR</i> (0.583&lt;<i>WAIR</i>≤0.624&nbsp;Å) is beneficial to the formation of multiphase materials dominated by P2 phase; while a larger <i>WAIR</i> (0.624&lt;<i>WAIR</i>&lt;0.638&nbsp;Å) leads to the composition of major O3 and minor P2 phases. The larger <i>WAIR</i> is caused by the increase of TMs with a larger ionic radius at the TM site, resulting in a shorter distance between the oxygen layers. Therefore, the repulsion between oxygen layers increases and the material tends to form an O3 structure, which is consistent with the results described in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0001">1b</a>. That is, by adjusting the <i>WAIR</i> value, it is possible to approximately control the dominant phase (P2 or O3 phase) in the multiphase materials. At the same time, it is observed that the phase proportion is also affected by the content of TM. Under the same <i>WAIR</i> values of 0.596, 0.600, 0.601, 0.602, 0.621, 0.622, 0.625, 0.626, and 0.627&nbsp;Å, more O3 phase is observed with the increase of Ni content(orange squares in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0001">1c</a>). This is reasonable, since NiO possesses the same space group(R-3m) with O3 phase,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0041_R_d66350119e944" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Colloid Interface Sci. J. Mater. Chem. A">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> unlike the P6<sub>3</sub>/mmc space group of P2 phase. Within the similar Ni content of 20–23%, the gradual increase of <i>WAIR</i> from 0.622 to 0.629 Å leads to the rise of the XRD signal from O3 at the expense of P2 phase (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0001">1e</a>). These features verify that both <i>WAIR</i> and TM ratios are influential for the phase composition in multiphase structures.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400127-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/716ae8ac-5c5a-4494-b308-15475fed2fba/aenm202400127-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/716ae8ac-5c5a-4494-b308-15475fed2fba/aenm202400127-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/885827e2-51bd-4de4-ab73-782ba57cd108/aenm202400127-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/716ae8ac-5c5a-4494-b308-15475fed2fba/aenm202400127-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400127-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400127" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Different compositions of TM and the corresponding phase structures (S<sub>1</sub>–S<sub>43</sub> are corresponding to samples 1–43). b) Schematic illustration of the relationship between TM size and structure. c) Collected phase structures and <i>WAIR</i> of TMs for the 43 different compositions in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0001">1a</a>. d) X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns of the HE multiphase materials with different Ni content. e) X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns of the HE multiphase materials with different <i>WAIR</i>.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Based on the findings above, other compositions with five and six different components were also tested for the formation of phase structures in HE composites. Different valence metals (Mg<sup>2+</sup>, Fe<sup>3+</sup>, Al<sup>3+</sup>, Mo<sup>6+</sup>) were chosen to replace one or more metals in Ni/Mn/Cu/Ti/Sn components randomly to adjust the <i>WAIR</i> between 0.583–0.638&nbsp;Å. The five TM of Na<sub>0.67</sub>Ni<sub>0.23</sub>Mn<sub>0.56</sub>Ti<sub>0.06</sub>Mg<sub>0.1</sub>Sn<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (<i>WAIR</i> = 0.598&nbsp;Å), Na<sub>0.66</sub>Ni<sub>0.25</sub>Mn<sub>0.58</sub>Cu<sub>0.1</sub>Mo<sub>0.02</sub>Sn<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (<i>WAIR</i> = 0.599&nbsp;Å), Na<sub>0.73</sub>Mn<sub>0.4</sub>Cu<sub>0.08</sub>Mg<sub>0.05</sub>Al<sub>0.05</sub>Fe<sub>0.42</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (<i>WAIR</i> = 0.601&nbsp;Å) and Na<sub>0.75</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.55</sub>Cu<sub>0.1</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Zn<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (<i>WAIR</i> = 0.603&nbsp;Å) display multiphase of P2 and O3 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6a</a>, Supporting Information), with the P2 as a majority and O3 as a minority. Furthermore, the six TM contained Na<sub>0.75</sub>Ni<sub>0.05</sub>Mn<sub>0.4</sub>Cu<sub>0.08</sub>Mg<sub>0.05</sub>Al<sub>0.05</sub>Fe<sub>0.37</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.73</sub>Ni<sub>0.28</sub>Mn<sub>0.4</sub>Cu<sub>0.05</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>Sn<sub>0.1</sub>Fe<sub>0.07</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with the individual <i>WAIRs</i> of 0.604 and 0.616 Å also generate the HE structures with P2 as the majority phase. Meanwhile, the six TM contained Na<sub>0.75</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.3</sub>Cu<sub>0.13</sub>Ti<sub>0.12</sub>Mg<sub>0.12</sub>Sn<sub>0.12</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with the <i>WAIR</i> of 0.633 Å showing a strong layered structure of O3, only with very tiny diffraction singles from P2 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6b</a>, Supporting Information). These phenomena further prove the above conclusion that <i>WAIR</i> in 0.583&lt;<i>WAIR</i>≤0.624 Å is conducive to the formation of P2 main phase; while <i>WAIR</i> in 0.624&lt;<i>WAIR</i>&lt;0.638 Å results in the composition of the major O3 phase. In these new components (Ni/Mn/Cu/Mo/Sn and Ni/Mn/Cu/Ti/Fe/Sn) generated structures, when remaining the <i>WAIR</i> values constant, the XRD signal from O3 phase also increases with the increase of Ni (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7a,b</a>, Supporting Information), further verifying that the high Ni content leads to the rise of O3 phase. It is consistent with the previous conclusion in Ni/Mn/Cu/Ti/Sn composed structures. In addition, all the elements in these five- and six-TMs composed structures are uniformly distributed on the particles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information), implying the formation of multiple elements coexisted structures. The generation of HE and the alternation of phase structures of these above five- and six-TMs composed structures further confirms the hypothesis that the formation of multiphase structures in HE is affected by the <i>WAIR</i> of TMs.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202400127-sec-0040">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202400127-sec-0040-title">2.2 Structural Properties of HE Multiphase Structures</h3>
            
            <p>To better investigate the structure of HE and multiphase materials, low-entropy (LE) multiphase, HE multiphase and HE single-phase materials were employed for comparison (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0002">2a</a>). Among these above mentioned 43 multiphase materials, Na<sub>0.75</sub>Ni<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.4</sub>Cu<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.12</sub>Sn<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (Δ<i>S</i><sub>c<i>onfig</i></sub> = 1.58R&gt;1.5R, denoted as HE-P2/O3) is selected as the representative due to the relatively higher Ni content and higher theoretical capacity. HE-P2/O3 is compared with LE multiphase P2/O3-Na<sub>0.75</sub>Ni<sub>0.35</sub>Mn<sub>0.6</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (Δ<i>S</i><sub>c<i>onfig</i></sub> = 0.89R&lt;1R, denoted as LE-P2/O3) to reveal the function of HE, and is compared with HE single-phase O3-Na<sub>0.67</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.25</sub>Cu<sub>0.13</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>Sn<sub>0.22</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (Δ<i>S</i><sub>c<i>onfig</i></sub> = 1.85R&gt;1.5R, denoted as HE-O3) to demonstrate the effect of multiphase. LE-P2/O3 is chosen because it possesses the same multiphase structure (P2 and O3) and the same Na content as HE-P2/O3, while only the entropy configurations are different, allowing direct comparison of the entropy on the structure. Similarly, HE-O3 owns the same entropy configurations as HE-P2/O3, but shows a single-phase, providing an example for understanding the role of multiphase. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0002">2b</a>, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, and Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>–<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information), compared with the LE-P2/O3, the (0 0 3) and (0 0 2) peaks of HE-P2/O3 and the (0 0 3) peak of HE-O3 appear in a lower angle, indicating a larger c value in HE cathodes. In the HE-P2/O3, the obtained lattice parameters are c = 16.46 Å, V = 125.1 Å<sup>3</sup> for O3 phase and c = 11.21 Å, V = 82.3 Å<sup>3</sup> for P2 phase, which are larger than that of LE-P2/O3 (c = 16.3113 Å, V = 120.9 Å<sup>3</sup> in O3 phase and c = 11.13 Å, V = 80.6 Å<sup>3</sup> in P2 phase), as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0002">2c</a>. The increased parameters indicate multiple elements have entered the lattice, and the lattice parameters could be optimized using a larger radius Ni/Cu/Ti/Sn to replace Mn (r<sub>Cu</sub><sup>2+</sup> = 0.73 Å, r<sub>Ti</sub><sup>4+</sup> = 0.605 Å, r<sub>Sn</sub><sup>4+</sup> = 0.69 Å, r<sub>Ni</sub><sup>2+</sup> = 0.69 Å vs r<sub>Mn</sub><sup>4+</sup> = 0.53 Å). Compared HE-P2/O3 with HE-O3, XRD patterns of HE-P2/O3 match well with the combination of P6<sub>3</sub>/mmc space group of P2 phase and R-3m space group of O3 phase; while in HE-O3, all the diffraction peaks are only in one space group of R-3m for O3 phase. The HE-P2/O3 contains two types of structures of 76.61% O3 phase and 23.39% P2 phase, which provides two Na<sup>+</sup>-migration channels compared with only one Na<sup>+</sup>-migration channel in HE-O3 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0002">2d</a>). In the LE-P2/O3, the P2 and O3 phases take account of 68.59% and 31.41%, respectively. The triangular prism site of P2 phase in P2/O3 provides a wider Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion channel than the single octahedral site in O3, indicating the multiphase provides more opportunities for the Na<sup>+</sup> migration. Compared with LE-P2/O3, the Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy ordering peak at ≈28° vanished in HE-P2/O3 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information), indicating the ordered Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy arrangement is reduced with the formation of HE, which is beneficial to the Na<sup>+</sup> migration.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0027_R_d66350119e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Power Sources Sci. Adv. J. Am. Chem. Soc.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the diverse phases in P2/O3 are favorable to relieve the stress and alleviate the interlayer gliding of TMO<sub>2</sub> during Na<sup>+</sup>-intercalation/extraction, due to the constraint effect from different lattice orientations in one particle.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0040_R_d66350119e1298" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Combined with the multiphase, disordered Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy arrangement, and the increased c parameter owing to the multi-elemental doping, the HE-P2/O3 should possess improved Na<sup>+</sup>-migration capability.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400127-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7fdceee1-ad4e-4365-9d35-9d979b71eff3/aenm202400127-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/7fdceee1-ad4e-4365-9d35-9d979b71eff3/aenm202400127-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0ceea061-5eaa-4eca-b7b6-e4ec7148f48d/aenm202400127-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7fdceee1-ad4e-4365-9d35-9d979b71eff3/aenm202400127-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400127-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400127" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Comparison among LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3 and HE-O3. b) XRD patterns comparison of LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3, HE-O3 and the partially enlarged area of (0 0 3) and (0 0 2) peaks (Red vertical line corresponds to P2 phase PDF#54-0894, green vertical line corresponds to O3 phase PDF#54-0887). c) Changes in lattice parameter c and volume V. d) Schematic illustrations of the structural difference between HE-P2/O3 and HE-O3.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The crystal structures of these compounds were visualized by high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM). As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0003">3a</a>, two sets of lattice fringes in different orientations with the interlayer distances of 0.53 and 0.23&nbsp;nm are observed in LE-P2/O3, associated with the (0 0 3) plane of O3 phase and (1 0 0) plane of P2 phase, respectively. The corresponding diffraction spots also matched well with the O3 and P2 phases, confirming the coexistence of multiphase in one particle. The energy-dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) exhibits the uniform distribution of Na, Mn, Ni, and O on the particle (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0003">3b</a>). HRTEM image of HE-P2/O3 in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0003">3c</a> also displays two different lattice spacings of 0.54 and 0.24&nbsp;nm, matching well with the (0 0 3) plane of O3 phase and (1 0 0) plane of P2 phase, which are slightly larger than that in LE-P2/O3 and are consistent with the phenomenon that the XRD peak of (0 0 3) in HE-P2/O3 shift to left compared with LE-P2/O3 sample, due to larger radius ions‘ doping and a larger c parameter (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0002">2b</a>). The EDS mapping shows the homogeneous distribution of Na, Ni, Mn, Cu, Ti, Sn, and O elements, indicating the successful preparation of HE configuration. A single lattice fringe with a uniform spacing of 0.54&nbsp;nm appeared in HE-O3, corresponding to the (0 0 3) plane of O3 phase. The elements of Na, Ni, Mn, Cu, Ti, Sn, and O are uniformly distributed on the particle implying the formation of HE single O3 phase structure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0003">3e</a>). Through comparing the above three structures, the HE-P2/O3 own a wider lattice interlayer distance than LE-P2/O3 and a more staggered phase arrangement compared with the single phase HE-O3 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information), which are conducive to the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> and the suppression of interlayer gliding during charge–discharge process owing to the different lattice orientations.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400127-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/503225a3-1b20-458f-8d15-21e26ad81520/aenm202400127-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/503225a3-1b20-458f-8d15-21e26ad81520/aenm202400127-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/163a67ff-809d-4720-acfc-6f83bc3bdf5b/aenm202400127-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/503225a3-1b20-458f-8d15-21e26ad81520/aenm202400127-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400127-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400127" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">High-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) images and corresponding signal profiles of the regions marked with blue and orange boxes in the a) LE-P2/O3, c) HE-P2/O3 and e) HE-O3 (blue square corresponds to O3 phase, orange square corresponds to P2 phase). Energy-dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) elemental mapping of b) LE-P2/O3, d) HE-P2/O3, f) HE-O3 materials.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202400127-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202400127-sec-0050-title">2.3 Electrochemical Performance of HE Multiphase Structures</h3>
            
            <p>To explore the effect of HE and multiphase on the electrochemical performance of SIBs, LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3, and HE-O3 were evaluated in half cells with Na metal as anode. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0004">4a</a> shows the initial charge–discharge profiles of these three kinds of materials in a voltage range of 2.0–4.5&nbsp;V at a current density of 10&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. HE-P2/O3 cathode delivers an initial capacity of 150.0&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, while LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 electrodes exhibit initial capacities of 151.4 and 109.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. It is observed that the HE-P2/O3 delivers higher capacity than HE-O3, which can be attributed to the increased Ni-content in HE-P2/O3(33%) than HE-O3(20%) and so more Na<sup>+</sup>-extraction. In addition, the HE-P2/O3 delivered an initial Coulombic efficiency of 107%, higher than that of HE-O3(90.3%), which can be attributed to more Na<sup>+</sup>-vacancy during the formation of P2-phase and more extra Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption/intercalation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0041_R_d66350119e1401" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Colloid Interface Sci. J. Mater. Chem. A">41</a>, <a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0042_R_d66350119e1401" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Ind. Eng. Chem. Res.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Although both LE-P2/O3 and HE-P2/O3 contain multiphases of P2 and O3, the charge–discharge profiles of HE-P2/O3 are smoother than that of LE-P2/O3, indicating that the Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy orderliness is effectively inhibited due to the presence of multicomponents in HE(Ni/Mn/Cu/Ti/Sn) structures. The CV curves of LE-P2/O3 show clearly separated multiple redox peaks with sharp peak shapes, corresponding to the multiple steps in the charge–discharge. In contrast, in the HE electrodes (HE-P2/O3 and HE-O3), the redox peaks are integrated and broader, indicating the HE composition suppressed the Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy ordering (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). Because the suppression of Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy ordering can lead to a wider range of complete solid-solution behavior, resulting in broadening the redox peaks<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0027_R_d66350119e1416" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Power Sources Sci. Adv. J. Am. Chem. Soc.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>. In long cycling (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0004">4b</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information), the HE-P2/O3 exhibits better cycling stability with a capacity retention of 77.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 300 cycles, while the capacity shows severe decay in LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 with the retention of 19.9 and 35.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 300th cycle, respectively.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400127-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f875ea89-2cb3-4767-a583-7af8d6fe6456/aenm202400127-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/f875ea89-2cb3-4767-a583-7af8d6fe6456/aenm202400127-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/06e6f319-e4cd-4aea-a02c-69170ff2a912/aenm202400127-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f875ea89-2cb3-4767-a583-7af8d6fe6456/aenm202400127-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400127-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400127" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The initial charge–discharge profiles of LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3, and HE-O3 at 10&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> within 2.0–4.5&nbsp;V. b) Cycling performance at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2.0–4.5&nbsp;V. c) The rate performance of three electrodes at different current densities. d) Comparison of D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> among LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3, and HE-O3 in the first cycle based on GITT tests (Galvanostatic Intermittent Titration Technique). e) Cycling performance of LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3-α, HE-P2/O3-β, HE-P2/O3, and HE-O3.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>For the rate capability (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0004">4c</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information), the HE-P2/O3 show similar capacities with LE-P2/O3 at initial three cycles in a relatively lower current density of 10&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, both of which are obviously higher than that of HE-O3. This can be attributed to a larger lattice interlayer distance in P2 than O3. With the rise of current in the following cycles, the capacities of LE-P2/O3 become gradually lower than that of HE-P2/O3, possibly owing to poorer cycling stability of LE-P2/O3, especially considering more P2 content in LE-P2/O3(68.59%) than in HE-P2/O3(23.39%). At a high current density of 750&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the HE-P2/O3 still delivers a discharge capacity of 88.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, significantly higher than that of HE-O3 (44.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). In addition, both HE-P2/O3 and LE-P2/O3 exhibit obviously higher Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>) than HE-O3 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0004">4d</a>; Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>–<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a>, Supporting Information), due to the existence of a triangular prism channel of P2 phase, which has wider Na<sup>+</sup> channel than O3 phase. In the high-voltage region of 4.0–4.5&nbsp;V, the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of all three materials undergo a decline sharply, but the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of HE-P2/O3 is still higher than that of LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0004">4d</a>). This may be associated with the absence of P2→O2 phase transition and a larger lattice interlayer distance in P2 phase. In addition, HE-P2/O3 exhibits lower charge transfer resistance (R<sub>CT</sub>) than those of LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 (150&nbsp;Ω&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup> vs 200 and 265&nbsp;Ω&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>), which can be attributed to the combination of HE (optimized lattice parameters) and multiphase (different lattice orientations) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information). When the current density returns to 10&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacities of HE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 recover to 149.4 and 110.0&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, near the corresponding initial values. However, the LE-P2/O3 only delivers a capacity of 126.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which is obviously lower than the initial capacity of 151.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. These phenomena indicate that HE is also conducive to structural reversibility.</p>
            
            <p>Other HE multiphase cathodes of Na<sub>0.67</sub>Ni<sub>0.28</sub>Cu<sub>0.05</sub>Mn<sub>0.57</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>Sn<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (HE-P2/O3-α) and Na<sub>0.7</sub>Ni<sub>0.3</sub>Cu<sub>0.05</sub>Mn<sub>0.45</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>Sn<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (HE-P2/O3-β) have also been tested (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0004">4e</a>). The capacities retain 63.1 and 70.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 200 cycles, which are also higher than that of LE-P2/O3 (35.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and HE-O3 (45.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). The improved cycling performance of all these HE multiphase cathodes can be attributed to the synergistic function of HE and multiphase, which achieve a balance between cycling stability and high capacity. At a small current density of 10&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with sufficient electrode reaction, HE multiphase cathodes also show better cycling stability than LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information). Under gradually narrowed voltage windows of 2.0–4.4, 2.0–4.3, 2.0–4.2, and 2.0–4.1&nbsp;V, the cycling performance is improved obviously (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information). After 300 cycles, the capacity retention of HE-P2/O3 increased from 68.4% of 4.5&nbsp;V to 76.6% of 4.4&nbsp;V, 79.6% of 4.3&nbsp;V, 92.8% of 4.2&nbsp;V, and 95.5% of 4.1&nbsp;V, respectively. Meanwhile, the cycling stability of HE-P2/O3 maintains better in different voltage windows compared with LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21i</a>, Supporting Information), further verifying the structural superiority of HE-P2/O3 during repeated Na<sup>+</sup>-extraction and intercalation. Moreover, compared with the previously reported cycling performance of layered cathodes (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information), under the same conditions, HE-P2/O3 exhibits a slightly superior or comparable performance level.</p>
            
            <p>X-ray absorption fine structure (XAFS) measurement is performed to evaluate the redox behavior of Ni, Mn, Cu, and Ti in HE-P2/O3 at different voltages, as shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0005">5</a>. The normalized X-ray absorption near edge structure (XANES) spectra of TM in pristine HE-P2/O3 electrodes match well with NiO, MnO<sub>2</sub>, CuO, and TiO<sub>2</sub>, corresponding to Ni<sup>2+</sup>, Mn<sup>4+</sup>, Cu<sup>2+</sup>, and Ti<sup>4+</sup>, respectively. When charging to 4.5&nbsp;V, the K-edge XANES spectra of Ni shift to higher energy with an increment of ≈3&nbsp;eV compared with the pristine state (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0005">5a</a>), revealing the oxidization of Ni<sup>2+</sup> to Ni<sup>4+</sup>. After discharge to 2.0&nbsp;V, the Ni XANES spectrum shifts negatively and returns to its original position, indicating a high reversibility of Ni<sup>2+/4+</sup> redox pairs. In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0005">5b</a>, Mn K-edge shows no apparent change during the charging process, but displays a slight shift to lower energy at the fully discharged state compared with the pristine state, demonstrating a slight reduction of Mn<sup>4+</sup> to Mn<sup>3+</sup>; while the majority of Mn is still maintained at +4. As for K-edge XANES of Cu and Ti, the curves overlap well with that of the pristine state in the first charge–discharge process, demonstrating the valence state remains constant in HE-P2/O3. The Fourier-transformed extended X-ray absorption fine structures (FT-EXAFS) at Ni and Mn K-edge are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0005">5e,f</a>. The Ni-O peak significantly shrinks with the oxidation of Ni<sup>2+</sup> to Ni<sup>4+</sup> in the charging process due to a smaller ionic radius of Ni<sup>4+</sup> than Ni<sup>2+</sup>, which extends to the original position during the discharge process. No apparent shifts are observed in Mn-O, indicating the preservation of bond lengths, which is beneficial to maintaining the structure stability during cycling. These features are consistent with the results of the X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) test (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a>, Supporting Information). The Ni 2p peaks shift from 855.4&nbsp;eV (Ni 2p<sub>3/2</sub>) and 873.3&nbsp;eV (Ni 2p<sub>1/2</sub>) to 857.5 and 876.1&nbsp;eV when charging to 4.5&nbsp;V, which then return to the original positions, indicating a reversible redox reaction of Ni<sup>2+</sup>↔Ni<sup>4+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0043_R_d66350119e1644" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Adv. Energy Mater.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Mn2p peaks at 642.8&nbsp;eV (Mn 2p<sub>3/2</sub>) and 654.3&nbsp;eV (Mn 2p<sub>1/2</sub>) stay unchanged in the charging process, but the peaks of Mn2p shift to lower energy values at 641.7 (Mn 2p<sub>3/2</sub>) and 653.5&nbsp;eV (Mn 2p<sub>1/2</sub>) after discharging to 2.0&nbsp;V, implying partial Mn<sup>4+</sup> is reduced to Mn<sup>3+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0044_R_d66350119e1662" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Electrochim. Acta">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the case of Ti, Cu, and Sn, no obvious shift is observed, indicating the valence preservation of these TM during the Na<sup>+</sup> extraction-insertion process. Therefore, in HE-P2/O3, the capacity is mainly contributed by the redox pairs of Ni<sup>2+</sup>→Ni<sup>4+</sup> and a little Mn<sup>3+</sup>→Mn<sup>4+</sup>. The doping elements of Ti<sup>4+</sup>, Cu<sup>2+</sup>, and Sn<sup>4+</sup> are electrochemically inactive, but are beneficial to maintain structural stability.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400127-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d2981340-3082-4f2c-8063-cb6164ecf50d/aenm202400127-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/d2981340-3082-4f2c-8063-cb6164ecf50d/aenm202400127-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/45b03afb-858d-4af6-9b64-b672be665272/aenm202400127-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/d2981340-3082-4f2c-8063-cb6164ecf50d/aenm202400127-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400127-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400127" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Normalized ex-situ XANES spectra at the a) Ni K-edge, b) Mn K-edge, c) Cu K-edge, and d) Ti K-edge of HE-P2/O3 electrode collected at different charge–discharge states and tested in an inert atmosphere, with the corresponding metal oxide as standard references. Corresponding Fourier transformed EXAFS spectra at the e) Ni K-edge and f) Mn K-edge (Ch-4.5 V: charge to 4.5&nbsp;V, Dis-2.0 V: discharge to 2.0&nbsp;V, FT: Fourier transform, Ni-TM: second coordination shells between Ni and transition metal, Mn-TM: second coordination shells between Mn and transition metal).</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202400127-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202400127-sec-0060-title">2.4 Structure and Stress Evolution in Cathodes</h3>
            
            <p>To elucidate the influence of HE and multiphase on the structure evolution during the charge–discharge process, ex-situ XRD measurements are performed on LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3, and HE-O3. As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0006">6a</a> and Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information), with the gradual extraction of Na<sup>+</sup>, (0 0 2) and (0 0 3) peaks of HE-P2/O3 shift to lower angles, corresponding to the expansion of the lattice parameter c with the progressively increased repulsion between TMO<sub>2</sub> layer. The (0 0 3) peak gradually weakens and completely disappears at 3.6&nbsp;V, which can be attributed to the phase transition of O3→P3. In addition, the diminishing intensity of (1 0 4) peak, accompanied by the enhancement of the (0 1 5) peak, further suggests the formation of the P3 phase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0045_R_d66350119e1731" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - J. Mater. Chem. A">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> When charged to the end state of 4.3–4.5&nbsp;V, P2 and P3 phases are still maintained without new peaks from other phases, indicating no phase transformation at the high voltage region. During the discharge process, a completely reversible phase transition from P2+P3 to P2+O3 is observed, in which, all diffraction peaks of P2 and O3 return to the initial states. However, the changing trend is different in the LE-P2/O3 cathode. The (0 0 3) peak completely disappears at 3.4&nbsp;V, which is lower than that of HE-P2/O3 (3.6&nbsp;V). Then a strong diffraction peak at 20.0° emerges when charging to 4.3&nbsp;V and the intensity gradually increases when further charging to 4.5&nbsp;V, indicating the phase transformation of P2 to O2, which is unfavorable for maintaining the structural stability (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0046_R_d66350119e1739" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Batteries Supercaps">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Among these three structures, the maximal change of lattice parameter c varies from 18.46% of the P2 phase in the LE-P2/O3 to 3.05% of HE-P2/O3 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0006">6b–d</a>). These large variations in lattice would cause anisotropic stress and cracks, deteriorating the long-term cycling. It is worth mentioning that none of these phase transitions occurs in HE-P2/O3 between 4.3 and 4.5&nbsp;V. As for the HE-O3 cathode, it undergoes a phase evolution from O3 to P3 phase, similar to that in HE-P2/O3, but the (0 0 3) peak becomes weaker and broader at 4.5&nbsp;V, indicating the crystallinity becomes poorer in fully charged state (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a>, Supporting Information), which is not observed in HE-P2/O3. This phenomenon can be attributed to the mutual support between different phases in HE-P2/O3, which is absent in single-phase HE-O3 and causes the interlayer gliding.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400127-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3f7f9dec-24cc-4576-8dc0-3f878ad17928/aenm202400127-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/3f7f9dec-24cc-4576-8dc0-3f878ad17928/aenm202400127-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4f61011d-d9c6-492c-8206-679e65a50159/aenm202400127-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3f7f9dec-24cc-4576-8dc0-3f878ad17928/aenm202400127-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400127-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400127" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The ex-situ XRD patterns (left) and the initial charge–discharge profiles (right) of HE-P2/O3 at different voltages in 2.0-4.5&nbsp;V (Ch-3.1 V: charge to 3.1&nbsp;V, Dis-4.1 V: discharge to 4.1&nbsp;V). The XRD samples were sealed in a polyimide device to avoid air contact. The changes of lattice parameter c in b) LE-P2/O3, c) HE-O3, and d) HE-P2/O3. Illustration of corresponding crystal structure evolutions of e) LE-P2/O3, f) HE-O3, and g) HE-P2/O3.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>For a better comparison, the structural evolution of LE-P2/O3, HE-O3, and HE-P2/O3 are illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0006">6e–g</a>. Compared with LE-P2/O3, the transformation of O3 to P3 in HE-P2/O3 is delayed by 0.2&nbsp;V and there is no O2 phase diffraction detected (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting Information), indicating that HE postpones the phase transition in low-voltage and suppresses the phase transition of P2 to O2 in high-voltage. In the HE composite of Ni/Mn/Cu/Ti/Sn, electrochemically active and inactive elements are randomly distributed in the TMO<sub>2</sub> layer, facilitating the stabilization of the layered structure during Na<sup>+</sup>-extraction/intercalation. Compared HE-P2/O3 with HE-O3, two different structures (76.61% for O3 phase and 23.39% for P2 phase) are interlaced in HE-P2/O3, which show different lattice orientations and are beneficial to suppress the interlayer gliding during Na<sup>+</sup> insertion and extraction. Therefore, in HE-P2/O3, the combination of HE (more inert elements in composition) and multiphase (more diversity in structure) facilitates to stabilization of the structure and so reaches better electrochemical performance.</p>
            
            <p>After 200 cycles, the P2 and O3 structures still preserve clearly in HE-P2/O3, but the intensities of (0 0 2) peak for P2 phase and (0 0 3) peak for O3 phase are decreased. On the other hand, the characteristic peak of O3 phase in LE-P2/O3 completely disappears after 100 cycles (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0007">7a–c</a>), indicating the contribution of HE in maintaining the structural stability. Under HRTEM, both the P2 and O3 phases lattice fringes of the cycled HE-P2/O3 still could be recognized clearly, verifying the long-term structural stability. However, for the LE-P2/O3 after 200 cycles, the lattice fringes of P3 phase are detected without obvious diffraction from the initial O3 phase, indicating the poor structural preservation capability during long-term cycling, owing to the irreversible phase transition. Not only structural stability but also long-term storage stability is important for potential applications. The LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3, and HE-O3 samples were exposed to air for 60 days and the structural change was monitored by XRD. The (0 0 3) peak of O3 phase in LE-P2/O3 composite gradually became weak and completely disappeared after 60 days (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0007">7d</a>). However, in HE composites of HE-P2/O3 and HE-O3, no significant change in (0 0 3) peak is detected (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0007">7e,f</a>), indicating better structural stability of HE-cathodes in the air, which is possibly associated with the structural stabilizing effect from multiple TM of Mn/Cu/Ti/Sn.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0012_R_d66350119e1800" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - J. Mater. Chem. A Nano Lett.">12</a>, <a href="#aenm202400127-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400127-bib-0013_R_d66350119e1800" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Ceram. Int. Adv. Mater.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400127-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d342660d-0e85-400e-adfe-6dc8d1ca41b0/aenm202400127-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/d342660d-0e85-400e-adfe-6dc8d1ca41b0/aenm202400127-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/5b0925dd-ced4-48f4-bd96-c097adfb466c/aenm202400127-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/d342660d-0e85-400e-adfe-6dc8d1ca41b0/aenm202400127-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400127-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400127" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">XRD patterns of a) LE-P2/O3, b) HE-P2/O3, and c) HE-O3 after 0, 25, 50, 75, 100, 150, and 200 cycles and corresponding HRTEM images after 200 cycles. XRD patterns of d) LE-P2/O3, e) HE-P2/O3, and f) HE-O3 after being exposed to air for different times.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>During charge–discharge, changes in Na<sup>+</sup> concentration and the accompanying phase transitions in cathode materials would lead to crystal expansion and shrinkage, resulting in anisotropic stress inside the particles. The Na<sup>+</sup> distribution and stress evolution in particles were simulated by COMSOL, as shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0008">8</a>. During Na<sup>+</sup> extraction, the Na<sup>+</sup> concentration becomes more inhomogeneous from surface to interior bulk in LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3. Whereas, in HE-P2/O3, the Na<sup>+</sup> concentration is more uniform due to higher Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics than that in LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0004">4d</a>). In addition, compared with LE-P2/O3, the P2→O2 phase transformation is also suppressed in HE-P2/O3 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0006">6a</a>). At the same charge voltage, the Na<sup>+</sup> concentration in LE-P2/O3 and HE-P2/O3 is smaller than HE-O3 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0008">8a–c</a>), further indicating the multiphase structures provide more chance for Na<sup>+</sup> extraction compared with the single-phase structure. The inhomogeneous Na<sup>+</sup> distribution and large volume changes are the critical driving forces of internal stress generation. The stress distribution of the LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3, and HE-O3 during charge–discharge are simulated and shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0008">8d–f</a>. In the charging process, the internal stress in all three compounds gradually increases with the inhomogeneous distribution of Na<sup>+</sup> and the generation of phase transitions. Due to the P2→O2 transition in LE-P2/O3, it shows the highest stress compared with HE-P2/O3 and HE-O3, reaching 113&nbsp;MPa at 4.5&nbsp;V, more than twice HE-P2/O3 (41&nbsp;MPa). During the discharge process, the stress undergoes a significant decrease, but the final state is different from the pristine state owing to some residual stress (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a>, Supporting Information). Among these three composites, residual stress in LE-P2/O3 is the severest of 6.9&nbsp;MPa. While, HE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 structures show obviously lower residual stress of 3.3 and 4.3&nbsp;MPa (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26b</a>, Supporting Information), respectively. These features can be attributed to the severe phase transition of P2→O2 in LE-P2/O3, which results in larger changes along the <i>c</i>-axis (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0006">6b–d</a>). During long-term cycling, the particles suffer from repeated changes of stress and gradual accumulation of deformation, causing the generation of intragranular cracks. The cross-sectional SEM images of cycled LE-P2/O3 show obvious cracks throughout the particle (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0008">8g</a>), creating a more exposed interface with electrolytes and aggravating the side reactions, leading to the degradation of the electrode. On the other hand, the HE-P2/O3 and HE-O3 particles do not show severe cracks after 200 cycles at the same condition, and the integrity of HE-P2/O3 is even better, verifying the relieved stress, in agreement with the simulation of internal stress (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400127-fig-0008">8h</a>). Therefore, the HE composition and multiphase are beneficial to the reduction of stress and so the preservation of particle integrity in the cathode materials.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400127-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/126677eb-b3fd-4959-a6a3-05c71354dd40/aenm202400127-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/126677eb-b3fd-4959-a6a3-05c71354dd40/aenm202400127-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/370e8981-dbd5-42e4-8565-f97ad1d1cf56/aenm202400127-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/126677eb-b3fd-4959-a6a3-05c71354dd40/aenm202400127-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400127-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400127" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The Na<sup>+</sup> concentration distribution simulation diagrams in the charging process of a) LE-P2/O3, b) HE-P2/O3, and c) HE-O3. The stress simulation diagram during the charge–discharge process of d) LE-P2/O3, e) HE-P2/O3, and f) HE-O3 (OCV: open circuit voltage, Ch-3.2 V: charge to 3.2&nbsp;V, Dis-3.4 V: discharge to 3.4&nbsp;V). Cross-sectional SEM images of g) LE-P2/O3, h) HE-P2/O3, and i) HE-O3 particles before and after 200 cycles.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202400127-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202400127-sec-0070-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In conclusion, 43 kinds of HE multiphase structures are prepared by refining the TM content, in which, the <i>WAIR</i> of TM is observed critical on the phase compositions. When <i>WAIR</i> is between 0.583 and 0.637&nbsp;Å, the multiphases containing P2 and O3 are formed, and the proportion of O3 phase increases with the rise of <i>WAIR</i>. LE-P2/O3, HE-P2/O3, and HE-O3 are investigated and compared to explore the effect of HE and multiphase on electrochemical properties. The HE multiphase cathode of HE-P2/O3 delivers a cycling stability of 77.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 300 cycles and a desired rate performance of 88.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 750&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which is significantly better than that of LE-P2/O3 and HE-O3, demonstrating the positive contribution of HE and multiphase. In HE-P2/O3, benefiting from the disordered distribution of inactive TM of Mn/Cu/Ti/Sn in TMO<sub>2</sub> layer, the O3→P3 phase transformation is restricted and the irreversible phase transformation of P2→O2 is suppressed as well. With the help of different lattice orientations of P2 and O3 phases in HE-P2/O3, the interlayer gliding is inhibited and so is favorable to cycling stability. In addition, HE multiphase materials show superiority in air stability and mechanical strength. This work revealed the regulations for the formation of multiphase HE cathodes and demonstrated the combined functions of HE and multiphase.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
